            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hollow carbon nanowires were prepd. by pyrolysis of a hollow polyaniline nanowire precursor.  The hollow carbon nanowires used as anode material for Na-ion batteries deliver a high reversible capacity of 251 mA-h/g and 82.2% capacity retention over 400 charge-discharge cycles between 1.2 and 0.01 V (vs. Na+/Na) at a const. current of 50 mA/g (0.2C).  Excellent cycling stability is also obsd. at an even higher charge-discharge rate.  A high reversible capacity of 149 mA-h/g also can be obtained at a current rate of 500 mA/g (2C).  The good Na-ion insertion property is attributed to the short diffusion distance in the hollow carbon nanowires and the large interlayer distance (0.37 nm) between the graphitic sheets, which agrees with the interlayered distance predicted by theor. calcns. to enable Na-ion insertion in carbon materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq9utH1EdajJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljM5ATGlei_IQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XotlShu78%253D&amp;md5=c54fcb809a340c023d9185f1d9f5e848</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref51" class="rightTabRefNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit51" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201902077"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, G.-T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Diemant, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Behm, R.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, a Mn-based metal-org. framework is used as a precursor to obtain well-defined a-MnS/S-doped C microrod composites.  Ultrasmall a-MnS nanoparticles (3-5 nm) uniformly embedded in S-doped carbonaceous mesoporous frameworks (a-MnS/SCMFs) are obtained in a simple sulfidation reaction.  As-obtained a-MnS/SCMFs shows outstanding lithium storage performance, with a specific capacity of 1383 mAh g-1 in the 300th cycle or 1500 mAh g-1 in the 120th cycle (at 200 mA g-1) using copper or nickel foil as the current collector, resp. Importantly, in situ X-ray diffraction measurements studies on electrodes employing various metal foils/disks as current collector reveal the occurrence of the conversion reaction of CuS at (de)lithiation process when using copper foil as the current collector.  This constitutes the first report of the reaction mechanism for a-MnS, eventually forming metallic Mn and Li2S.  In situ dilatometry measurements demonstrate that the peculiar structure of a-MnS/SCMFs effectively restrains the electrode vol. variation upon repeated (dis)charge processes.  Finally, a-MnS/SCMFs electrodes present an impressive performance when coupled in a full cell with com.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanocrystals with quantum-confined length scales are often considered impractical for metal-ion battery electrodes due to the dominance of solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) layer effects on the measured storage properties.  Here we demonstrate that ultrafine sizes (∼4.5 nm, av.) of iron pyrite, or FeS2, nanoparticles are advantageous to sustain reversible conversion reactions in sodium ion and lithium ion batteries.  This is attributed to a nanoparticle size comparable to or smaller than the diffusion length of Fe during cation exchange, yielding thermodynamically reversible nanodomains of converted Fe metal and NaxS or LixS conversion products.  This is compared to bulk-like electrode materials, where kinetic and thermodn. limitations of surface-nucleated conversion products inhibit successive conversion cycles.  Reversible capacities over 500 and 600 mAh/g for sodium and lithium storage are obsd. for ultrafine nanoparticles, with improved cycling and rate capability.  Unlike alloying or intercalation processes, where SEI effects limit the performance of ultrafine nanoparticles, our work highlights the benefit of quantum dot length-scale nanocrystal electrodes for nanoscale metal sulfide compds. that store energy through chem. conversion reactions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoQ5K7_RKr0B7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljM5ATGlei_IQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhslKlsbbL&amp;md5=04764f41c3057c65e1f434a6b7cca04a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref53" class="rightTabRefNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit53" data-doi="10.1038/nmat3601"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Augustyn, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Come, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lowe, M.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pseudocapacitance is commonly assocd. with surface or near-surface reversible redox reactions, as obsd. with RuO2·xH2O in an acidic electrolyte.  However, we recently demonstrated that a pseudocapacitive mechanism occurs when lithium ions are inserted into mesoporous and nanocrystal films of orthorhombic Nb2O5 (T-Nb2O5; refs , ).  Here, we quantify the kinetics of charge storage in T-Nb2O5: currents that vary inversely with time, charge-storage capacity that is mostly independent of rate, and redox peaks that exhibit small voltage offsets even at high rates.  We also define the structural characteristics necessary for this process, termed intercalation pseudocapacitance, which are a cryst. network that offers two-dimensional transport pathways and little structural change on intercalation.  The principal benefit realized from intercalation pseudocapacitance is that high levels of charge storage are achieved within short periods of time because there are no limitations from solid-state diffusion.  Thick electrodes (up to 40 μm thick) prepd. with T-Nb2O5 offer the promise of exploiting intercalation pseudocapacitance to obtain high-rate charge-storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPatnkXnvsNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lie28zCzFko1w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXlsl2jtL8%253D&amp;md5=ef16739fcf485430955b0414ac12f1ac</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref54" class="rightTabRefNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit54" data-doi="10.1016/j.xcrp.2020.100015"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ni, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Matios, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile-Processed Nanocarbon-Promoted Sulfur Cathode for Highly Stable Sodium-Sulfur Batteries</span>. <i>Cell Rep.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to the low cost and high energy d., the room temp. (RT) Na/S battery system is deemed as one of the best potential energy-storage systems.         </div><div class="casAbstract">For the design of light-metal-sulfur batteries and for the understanding of their performance, knowledge on the stable cryst. polysulfides is very important.  The authors confronted exptl. and ab initio crystal structure prediction studies on the stability of Na polysulfides.  The selected evolutionary-based structure-prediction algorithm was able to quickly and correctly predict the thermodynamically stable cryst. forms of Na polysulfides with small unit cells.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-metal sulfide battery holds great promise for sustainable and cost-effective applications.  Nevertheless, achieving high capacity and cycling stability remains a great challenge.  Here, uniform yolk-shell iron sulfide-carbon nanospheres have been synthesized as cathode materials for the emerging sodium sulfide battery to achieve remarkable capacity of ∼545 mA h g-1 over 100 cycles at 0.2 C (100 mA g-1), delivering ultrahigh energy d. of ∼438 Wh kg-1.  The proven conversion reaction between sodium and iron sulfide results in high capacity but severe vol. changes.  Nanostructural design, including of nanosized iron sulfide yolks (∼170 nm) with porous carbon shells (∼30 nm) and extra void space (∼20 nm) in between, has been used to achieve excellent cycling performance without sacrificing capacity.  This sustainable sodium-iron sulfide battery is a promising candidate for stationary energy storage.         ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bimetallic sulfides are prospective candidates as Na-ion battery (NIB) anodes owing to their abundant redox active sites and high specific capacities, while the rate and cycling performances are limited due to their severe mech. strain and sluggish reaction kinetics.  Herein, for the first time, a series of cubic spinel XIn2S4 (X = Fe, Co, Mn) anodes is proposed for superfast and ultrastable Na-ion storage.  The FeIn2S4 delivers the best electrochem. performance among them with the amazing results esp. for its superfast charging (9-13 s per charge with ≈300 mAh g-1 input) and ultrastable cycling capabilities (25 K cycles with ultralow 0.000801% capacity loss per cycle).  Further d. functional theory calcns. and exptl. results indicate that Fe substitution at tetrahedral sites of cubic spinel In2.77S4 can significantly enhance its elec. cond., Na-ion binding kinetics, and pseudocapacitive contributions, reduce its Na-ion diffusion barrier, and relieve its mech. strain.  Moreover, the inherent In skeleton at octahedral sites can induce a complementary reaction to stabilize the conversion-type Fe-based components.  Furthermore, the FeIn2S4-based full cells with excellent electrochem. performance are assembled.  This work demonstrates the feasibility of enhancing the synergies within bimetallic sulfides to realize remarkable electrochem. performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrX_7RNro94XrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lie28zCzFko1w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXitF2ntL3I&amp;md5=89ff995ca5c501bcb27f49a77ae6e7de</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i9">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acsami.3c12984?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsami.3c12984</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Experimental details including materials synthesis and characterization; XRD patterns of MnO<sub>2</sub>/ZIF-67 and MnO/Co/N–C; TEM images of Co–Mn–S@N–S–C; the size distribution of Co<sub>4</sub>S<sub>3</sub> nanoparticles; XRD patterns of Co<sub>4</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@N–S–C and MnS; Raman spectra of Co–Mn–S@N–S–C; TGA images of Co–Mn–S@N–S–C and XRD pattern of TGA residue; the nitrogen adsorption–desorption isotherms and pore size distribution curves; survey XPS spectra of Co–Mn–S@N–S–C, Co<sub>4</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@N–S–C, and MnS; high-resolution XPS spectra of Co<sub>4</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@N–S–C (C 1s, N 1s); CV curves of Co<sub>4</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@N–S–C and MnS electrodes for the first five cycles; galvanostatic charge–discharge profiles of Co<sub>4</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@N–S–C and MnS electrodes at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>; ex situ SEM image the Co–Mn–S@N–S–C electrode material before and after 50 cycles; galvanostatic charge–discharge profiles of Co<sub>4</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@N–S–C and MnS electrodes at different current densities; CV curves of Co<sub>4</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@N–S–C and MnS at different scan rates; the relationship between peak current and sweep rate of Co<sub>4</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@N–S–C and MnS; capacitive and diffusion-controlled contribution of Co<sub>4</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@N–S–C and MnS at 2.0 mV s<sup>–1</sup>; the normalized surface capacitive-controlled contribution ratio at different scan rates; and Nyquist plots of three electrodes before and after 100 cycles (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c12984/suppl_file/am3c12984_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c12984/suppl_file/am3c12984_si_001.pdf">am3c12984_si_001.pdf (1.33 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)

		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	});

	    e.preventDefault();

<script nonce="90f6e620da1a775c-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e620da1a775c-SJC">
"use strict"
//Script checks gdpr cookie and submits form
	/* 
	Create an in-page pop-up message, only for the InfoCentral homepage, that will gather email registrants for the library marketing list.
	 
	Needs the end point
	*/

var infoCentralCapture = (function() {

    //Detect mobile device
    window.mobilecheck = function() {
        var check = false;
        (function(a){if(/(android|bb\d+|meego).+mobile|avantgo|bada\/|blackberry|blazer|compal|elaine|fennec|hiptop|iemobile|ip(hone|od)|iris|kindle|lge |maemo|midp|mmp|mobile.+firefox|netfront|opera wa|abac|ac(er|oo|s\-)|ai(ko|rn)|al(av|ca|co)|amoi|an(ex|ny|yw)|aptu|ar(ch|go)|as(te|us)|attw|au(di|\-m|r |s )|avan|be(ck|ll|nq)|bi(lb|rd)|bl(ac|az)|br(e|v)w|bumb|bw\-(n|u)|c55\/|capi|ccwa|cdm\-|cell|chtm|cldc|cmd\-|co(mp|nd)|craw|da(it|ll|ng)|dbte|dc\-s|devi|dica|dmob|do(c|p)o|ds(12|\-d)|el(49|ai)|em(l2|ul)|er(ic|k0)|esl8|ez([4-7]0|os|wa|ze)|fetc|fly(\-|_)|g1 u|g560|gene|gf\-5|g\-mo|go(\.w|od)|gr(ad|un)|haie|hcit|hd\-(m|p|t)|hei\-|hi(pt|ta)|hp( i|ip)|hs\-c|ht(c(\-| |_|a|g|p|s|t)|tp)|hu(aw|tc)|i\-(20|go|ma)|i230|iac( |\-|\/)|ibro|idea|ig01|ikom|im1k|inno|ipaq|iris|ja(t|v)a|jbro|jemu|jigs|kddi|keji|kgt( |\/)|klon|kpt |kwc\-|kyo(c|k)|le(no|xi)|lg( g|\/(k|l|u)|50|54|\-[a-w])|libw|lynx|m1\-w|m3ga|m50\/|ma(te|ui|xo)|mc(01|21|ca)|m\-cr|me(rc|ri)|mi(o8|oa|ts)|mmef|mo(01|02|bi|de|do|t(\-| |o|v)|zz)|mt(50|p1|v )|mwbp|mywa|n10[0-2]|n20[2-3]|n30(0|2)|n50(0|2|5)|n7(0(0|1)|10)|ne((c|m)\-|on|tf|wf|wg|wt)|nok(6|i)|nzph|o2im|op(ti|wv)|oran|owg1|p800|pan(a|d|t)|pdxg|pg(13|\-([1-8]|c))|phil|pire|pl(ay|uc)|pn\-2|po(ck|rt|se)|prox|psio|pt\-g|qa\-a|qc(07|12|21|32|60|\-[2-7]|i\-)|qtek|r380|r600|raks|rim9|ro(ve|zo)|s55\/|sa(ge|ma|mm|ms|ny|va)|sc(01|h\-|oo|p\-)|sdk\/|se(c(\-|0|1)|47|mc|nd|ri)|sgh\-|shar|sie(\-|m)|sk\-0|sl(45|id)|sm(al|ar|b3|it|t5)|so(ft|ny)|sp(01|h\-|v\-|v )|sy(01|mb)|t2(18|50)|t6(00|10|18)|ta(gt|lk)|tcl\-|tdg\-|tel(i|m)|tim\-|t\-mo|to(pl|sh)|ts(70|m\-|m3|m5)|tx\-9|up(\.b|g1|si)|utst|v400|v750|veri|vi(rg|te)|vk(40|5[0-3]|\-v)|vm40|voda|vulc|vx(52|53|60|61|70|80|81|83|85|98)|w3c(\-| )|webc|whit|wi(g |nc|nw)|wmlb|wonu|x700|yas\-|your|zeto|zte\-/i.test(a.substr(0,4))) check = true;})(navigator.userAgent||navigator.vendor||window.opera);
              return check;
        };

    var _isMobile = window.mobilecheck();
    if (_isMobile) {
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').addClass('mobile');
    }

    var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage = "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

$(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
</script>


                    
                        



        
        <script nonce="90f6e620da1a775c-SJC">
var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>

$(document).ready(function(){
    var cookie = "";
    var uri = "/doi/full/10.1021/html_original_uri?id=123";
    console.log("ACSPubs2 start");
    $.getJSON('https://extreme-ip-lookup.com/json/', function(data, status) {
            if ( status == 'success' ) {
                $.each(data, function(i, field){
                    cookie=cookie.concat(i+' = '+field+" - ");
                });
                
            } else {
                    cookie=status;
            }

            cookie1 = cookie;
            cookie = cookie1 + "; path=/; domain=.acs.org";
            //document.cookie = "ACSPubs2= "+ btoa(cookie) ;
            $.cookie("ACSPubs2", btoa(cookie), {path: '/'}); // Session cookie valid across the entire site.
            //TODO send cookie val to the controller for logging
            console.log("ACSPubs2 success");
    })
    .fail(function(xx, status, err){
        cookie="error: 127.0.0.1";
        //document.cookie = "ACSPubs2= "+ btoa(cookie) ;
        $.cookie("ACSPubs2", btoa(cookie), {path: '/'}); // Session cookie valid across the entire site.
        console.log("ACSPubs2 failed");
        //TODO send cookie val to the controller for logging
    });
});    
</script>
